<text>Ambiance is a great lounge spot. My husband and I don't like packed clubs so it was nice to come, have drink and talk. There is a dance floor if you want to dance too. Beautiful black people everywhere.  Dress code is nice. No tennis shoes, tshirts or hats. I like that fact. I did see a few people out of code but I didn't care, I think a classy establishment needs a dress code that speaks to sophisticated individuals. Our bartender was awesome. The price of the drinks are average for downtown. Good lean though.  We kept ordering. No menu though. Waitresses and security were cool, polite, and friendly.  Only downfall is the cook wasn't there. I was hoping we could eat here too but we can try again another night. Also the bathroom is upstairs next door little odd if your drinking in heels.  I Loved it otherwise. My suggestion would be to have a specific menu for food and a couple crafted cocktails particular to the establishment. We had to go down the road for food and it was gross. So next time I am hoping to be able to eat there. And there is a cover charge after a certain time I don't know if it changes with the day or event. Not over priced though. We will definitely be going back. It was my husband's 30th birthday and he really enjoyed it.  He is hard to impress lol.<//text>< Pictures>

<text>In 2014, I took my son, a third grader, to get an orthodontic evaluation. During the consultation, Dr. Nicole pointed out my son long chin. Of course as a mom, I seen nothing wrong with my son. She ordered a lateral x-ray of his face. While my son was out of the room, Dr. Nicole preceded to ask me questions about my son; does he wake up often during the night? Does he have allergies? The questions continued, I stopped listening to her questions and focused on the past.

My eyes filled with tears, as she showed my son's lateral x-ray. His adenoids were enlarged pushing his chin downward & causing to block his airway.

Your probably wondering why I was so emotional. When my son was 2yrs old, after a week of being hospitalized, it took five doctors to come to a conclusion & diagnose my son with asthma. After his diagnosis, the hospital became our second home. He had a lot of asthma flare-ups. Almost every pulmonary x-rays were clear. He was given different medications. I am not sure if they even worked. I felt like the worst mom ever. Every time we visited the ER, I always felt attacked. My house looked like a pharmacy. One night, when I called 9-1-1 because my son was pale & having a hard time breathing. My son took a deep breath & yelled out to me "MOM! HELP ME! I NEED HELP! HELP ME MOM!" I cried uncontrollably because I wish I could take it all away. The paramedics got there and immediately gave him an epinephrine shot. He looked zoned out. That night he received two more epinephrine shots. Nothing was working. Again hospitalized. one occasion, I was asked to take a CPR class, just in case.

A few years of this routine, I was so upset. I yelled at the nurse, "this is ridiculous! We are always here! You guys make me feel like a bad mom! I'm doing everything you ask, and I am still here! THERE IS SOMETHING ELSE YOU GUYS ARE NOT DOING! So they ordered him an allergy test. After we got the results, we had to change our living conditions. Our house began to smell like cleaning products because he is allergic to dust & mold. We had to keep our pets outside. He was allergic dog & cat dander. I finally felt like something was getting done.

Boom! Another ER visit. What am I doing wrong? More tests were ordered. Many visits with the pulmonologist. I began to feel hopeless! The hospital bill's began to pile up. I was not working. My husband was in and out of jobs. Our financial situation was spiralling down. Obamacare was not ideal. Not qualify for medical, but had to chose between eating and getting my sons medication. Finally, my husband got a stable job & we were keeping up with mortgage. A few months later a blessing in disguise. My son teeth were so crooked. I felt we were financially stable to get him braces.

After our consultation, I got in my car & cried uncontrollably because Dr. Nicole had no idea what we have been through. This was my blessing. This was the prayer that was finally getting answered! After my son got his adenoids taken out, our lives, his life changed dramatically.

No more hospital visits. His medication was reduced or taken away. He read for a longer period of time. The list goes on, but the best part is that we can finally plan mini vacations without worry.

Getting my son's adenoids taken out, was the best thing that can ever happen to our lives. Thank you Dr. Nicole & the whole staff at Nalchajian Orthodontics!</text>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

< time>
1576719454700< /time>
<resp>None< /resp><review>A  "hole-in-the-wall" Hong Kong style cafe that can steal my heart any day. The place is frequented with the local elderly Chinese patrons so that means 2 things:

1) the food is a great taste Hong-Kong style classic meals (beef chow fun, baked pork chop rice, you know the deal)
2) the prices are cheap ($6-$10 are you kidding me?)

Yes, the place is cash only so do come prepared. As mentioned, this cafe is shabbier in interior decor. Manage your expectations with that and the service, which you shouldn't have too high of a standard for, especially with some language barrier.

They have special lunch specials with different dishes on each day of the week. ($6.15 includes a HK tea, which can be upgraded to a milk tea or any other of their cold drinks for .50 cents more)

I had the baked porkchop for $6.05 during their lunch hours (11am-3pm). The porkchop was juicy and tender, the sauce flavorful, and a hefty portion. I left quite happy. Parking can be difficult around here but usually there should be metered spots a block or two nearby.

I'll be back.</review>< Pics>
